I have the same problem with vitamin d. I feel i have all tre crucial information, maybe even more but not organized to point out my goal

3.1 Introduction 
Vitamin D History 1922
Vitamin D, often called the "sunshine vitamin", is synthesized in the skin through exposure to ultraviolet B (UVB, wavelength 290 - 315 nm) radiation from the sun. After UVB photons penetrate the skin and activate 7-dehydrocholesterol to previtamin D3 (photoconversion), which then isomerizes to vitamin D3 (cholecalciferol) (Holick, 2007). 
Vitamin D is the driver of a sophisticated system, called the “vitamin D endocrine system (VDES)”, and undergoes a two-step enzymatic activation (Norman, 2008). 
First, in the liver (cytochrome P450) it is hydroxylated by the enzyme 25-hydroxylase (CYP2R1) to form 25-hydroxyvitamin D [25(OH)D], the primary circulating form, and the major metabolite used to determine a patient's vitamin D status (Holick, 2006). 
Secondly, in the kidneys, 25(OH)D is taken up by the proximal renal tubules through endocytic internalization mediated by megalin and cubilin, which are members of the LDL receptor family (Nykjaer et al, 1999). 
Subsequently, in the proximal renal tubules, 25(OH)D is hydroxylated by the enzyme 1α-hydroxylase (CYP27B1) to 1,25-dihydroxyvitamin D [1,25(OH)₂D], the biologically active form of vitamin D, which exhibits simultaneously autocrine, paracrine and intracrine effects (DeLuca, 2004). 
24.25OH2D + 37 other metabolites. 
The enzyme 1α-hydroxylase is also expressed extra-renally in at least 17 types of cells (Kidd, 2010), extensively documented on placenta (Gray et al, 1979) and immune cells, like monocytes and macrophages (Stoffels et al., 2007; Esteban et al, 2004). 
1,25(OH)₂D exhibits simultaneously autocrine, paracrine and intracrine effects 
Hormone effect - secosteroid 
Vitamin D receptor (VDR), a member of the steroid/thyroid hormone nuclear receptors family with spontaneous presence in the cytosol, directly or indirectly affects many genes through transcriptional modifications (Strugnell & Deluca, 1997). Their importance is unequivocal, as 500 genes are estimated to be directly regulated by VDRs (Carleberg, 2003). 
VDR Structural Details
VDR is present across more than 38 types of tissues, controlling vital genes related to oxidative stress, inflammation and chronic diseases (Haussler et al., 2008).
 Vitamin D exerts its effect by binding to VDR, which heterodimerizes with the retinoid receptor (RXR), forming a complex that controls transcription of certain target genes (Jones et al., 1998).
Vitamin D binding protein (DBP) is a specific carrier of vitamin D and its metabolites, as almost all serum 25-hydroxyvitamin D is bound to circulating DBP. (Bouillon, 2001). 
 It has been found that more than 200 genes are directly or indirectly regulated by 1,25(OH)₂D, controlling cellular proliferation, differentiation, apoptosis, and angiogenesis (Nagpal & Rathnachalam, 2005).
While vitamin D is well known for its important function in bone health, it also significantly affects pancreatic beta cells, insulin sensitivity and secretion.
Vitamin D Regulatory Loops 
Vitamin D Activation and Action Diagram 
3.2 Vitamin D Mechanism of Action 
	In this section, we will explore the mechanisms implicated for vitamin D in major metabolic processes, particularly in the context of MetS. We highlight vitamin D importance in almost every pathophysiologic component of MetS, including insulin resistance, dyslipidemia, dysregulated immunity and hormonal balance. 
Vitamin D and Calcium 
Vitamin D’s regulation of calcium and phosphorus homeostasis is essential for bone health and normal mineralization. Vitamin D, 1,25(OH)₂D, mediates intestinal calcium absorption by activating of the synthesis of TRPV6 (a calcium channel) and facilitating transportation by tight-junction modification (Casadei et al., 2021; Mosali et al., 2014). Additionally, it increases renal tubular reabsorption of calcium, by enhancing the expression of calbindin and calcium transport in the distal convoluted tubule (Aguayo-Ruiz et al., 2020; Dusso et al., 2005).  Vitamin D deficiency, decreasing the availability of calcium, leads to structural defects that mimic osteoporosis (Levin et al., 1976). When administered, it effectively increases intestinal absorption of these important minerals and also promotes proper osteoblast function, further confirming its pleiotropic nature (Christakos et al, 2016). 
Parathyroid hormone (PTH) holds a primary role in regulating vitamin D activity by stimulating the transcription of 1αhydroxylase, thereby increasing production of 1,25(OH)₂D, which in turn provides negative feedback suppressing PTH synthesis and creating a loop (Christakos et al, 2010). Osteoblasts are activated by osteocalcin and PTH, which need vitamin D and K2 for proper function. PTH has also been implicated in insulin resistance, by reducing glucose uptake by liver, muscle and adipose cells (Thomas et al, 1995), while another study indicated that PTH decreased insulin-stimulated glucose uptake (Reusch et al, 1991).
VItamin D and Glucose 
Vitamin D is extensively involved in glucose metabolism, insulin production and insulin sensitivity, directly affecting the core metabolic dysfunction of MetS. 
A pivotal study by Ogunkolade et al. (2002) was one of the earliest works to demonstrate the association of vitamin D receptor polymorphism with insulin secretory capacity. Notably, 1,25-(OH)2D acts as an activator of the human insulin gene, playing an essential role in its transcription and subsequent excretion (Maestro et al, 2002). 
By acting directly on pancreatic beta cells and insulin-sensitive tissues, Vitamin D reduces insulin resistance, enhancing receptor expression and responsiveness (Pittas et al, 2007). 
The positive role of vitamin D is mediated by improved pancreatic β-cells function, including direct stimulation of insulin production and secretion through the extended presence of vitamin D receptors (VDR) (Johnson et al, 1994).
 Additionally, by regulating the intracellular and extracellular calcium pool of β-cells, vitamin D deficiency may disrupt normal release of insulin (Sooy et al, 1999). Calcium homeostasis is also influenced by vitamin K2, suggesting a collaborative effect. 
Vitamin D Vascular Health
Vitamin D affects lipid metabolism at the genetic level, being involved both in lipid synthesis and clearance. Adequate levels of Vitamin D are associated with favorable lipid profiles, including lower triglycerides (Jorde et al, 2010).
 A potential mechanism for increased lipogenesis associated with vitamin D deficiency is mediated by elevated PTH secretion, which stimulates lipogenesis by promoting an influx of calcium into the adipocytes (McCarty & Thomas, 2003). PTH and osteocalcin are also regulated by vitamin K2. 
Vitamin D deficiency leads to upregulation of renin, a mechanism implicated in Metabolic Syndrome hypertension, proving its regulatory role in the renin-angiotensin-aldosterone system (RAAS) (Li et al, 2002). 

Vitamin D Inflammation
 Beyond bone health, vitamin D exhibits potent anti-inflammatory properties, influencing both the innate and adaptive immunity (Aranow, 2011).
 These anti-inflammatory effects are significant in the context of MetS, where low-grade inflammation is present. Additionally, vitamin D, found to affect proliferation and differentiation of cells, has been implicated in cancer prevention and CVD (Holcik & Chen, 2008).
Vitamin D exhibits immune-modulating effects by downregulating pro-inflammatory cytokines and upregulating anti-inflammatory cytokines, reducing chronic inflammation in adipose tissue and, thus, regulating a key component of metabolic syndrome (Guillot, 2010). 
Moreover, vitamin D deficiency is connected to increased activity of PPARγ and C/EBPα receptors, components that are involved in the maturation of pre-adipocytes, leading to increased volume of adipose tissue ready to accumulate fat (Wood, 2008). 

3.3 Vitamin D Population Status 
The status of vitamin D in the body is most commonly determined by measuring the concentration of circulating total serum  [25(OH)D] (Holick et al, 2011). 
Currently, different organizations have  different definitions of vitamin D deficiency. It is mostly agreed that the levels of serum 25(OH)D < 30 nmol/L (12 ng/mL) is considered vitamin D deficiency, levels of 30–50 nmol/L (12–20 ng/mL) indicate insufficiency, and levels ≥50 nmol/L (20 ng/mL) is considered as being sufficient (Ross et al, 2011).
 However, in response to increased  levels of circulating PTH, the Endocrine Society designated the threshold of vitamin D deficiency at ≤ 50 nmol/L (20 ng/mL), the threshold of vitamin D insufficiency at 50–75 nmol/L (20–30 ng/mL), the threshold of vitamin D sufficiency at ≥75 nmol/L (30 ng/mL) (Bouillon et al, 2017) . 
It has been estimated that more than 30-50% of the children and adult population are at risk of vitamin D Deficiency (Holick & Chen, 2008). 
Cui et al (2023) reported that  "globally, 15.7%, 47.9%, and 76.6% of participants had serum 25-hydroxyvitamin D levels less than 30, 50, and 75 nmol/L, respectively. 
Vitamin D Levels and Health Outcomes - Table 
Data from representative human studies indicate various thresholds for serum 25D levels associated with health outcomes (Kidd, 2010):
<8 ng/mL: Classic vitamin D deficiency—rickets or osteomalacia (Institute of Medicine [IOM], 1997).
<17.8 ng/mL: Increased risk for all-cause mortality (Melamed et al., 2008).
<24 ng/mL: Greater risk of death in patients receiving intensive care; patients had three times greater mortality rate than those with serum 25D >60 ng/mL (Lee et al., 2009).
30 ng/mL: Greater risk for depression among hospitalized subjects (Schneider et al., 2000).
32 ng/mL: Threshold for optimal calcium absorption from the intestine (Heaney, 2008).
38 ng/mL: Threshold for optimal neuromuscular performance (Bischoff-Ferrari et al., 2004).

Vitamin D Sug

### 35. **Tool:**

**Κατανόηση του προβλήματος**

Ο χρήστης αντιμετωπίζει το ίδιο πρόβλημα με το κεφάλαιο για τη βιταμίνη D, όπου όλα τα κρίσιμα στοιχεία υπάρχουν αλλά δεν είναι οργανωμένα για να υποδεικνύουν το στόχο.

**Επανασχεδιασμός του κεφαλαίου**

Ο χρήστης ζητάει βοήθεια για να οργανώσει και να επικεντρωθεί στο κεφάλαιο για τη βιταμίνη D, εναρμονίζοντας το με τους στόχους της ανασκόπησης και πιθανώς προτείνοντας περίγραμμα ή τρόπους αναδιοργάνωσής του.

**Αξιολόγηση και προτάσεις**

Αναγνωρίζω τη δυσκολία του χρήστη και αναλύω τον τρέχοντα διατάξεις. Προτείνω νέο περίγραμμα με στόχο την συγχρηματιστική δυνατότητα των βιταμινών D και K2 σε μεταβολικό σύνδρομο. Εστίαση στη συγκεκριμένη αναδιοργάνωση και ενίσχυση του περιεχομένου.

**Αναδιάρθρωση και εστίαση**

Η αναγνώριση της ανάγκης για καλύτερη οργάνωση του κεφαλαίου βιταμίνης D για να επικεντρωθεί στο συγχρηματιστικό δυναμικό των βιταμινών D και K2 σε μεταβολικό σύνδρομο είναι κρίσιμη. Προτείνει να τονιστούν οι σχέσεις της βιταμίνης D με τα συστατικά του MetS και να επικεντρωθεί σε μηχανισμούς και αποδεικτικά στοιχεία που σχετίζονται με το MetS.

**Επανασχεδιασμός κεφαλαίου**

Ξεκινώ με μια σύντομη εισαγωγή για τη βιταμίνη D και διαρθρώνω το περιεχόμενο γύρω από θεματικές που συνδέουν άμεσα τη βιταμίνη D με τα συστατικά του μεταβολικού συνδρόμου. Χρησιμοποιώ υποκεφαλίδες για καλύτερη αναγνωσιμότητα και επικεντρώνομαι σε μηχανισμούς και αποδεικτικά στοιχεία που σχετίζονται με το MetS.

**Συγγραφική εναρμόνιση**

Η σύνοψη του ρόλου της βιταμίνης D και η σύνδεσή της με τη βιταμίνη K2 δημιουργεί μια συνέχεια στο αφήγημα. Το αναθεωρημένο περίγραμμα καλύπτει σύντομη εισαγωγή, μεταβολισμό, μηχανισμούς δράσης για Glucose, Inflammation, Lipid και BP.

**Έρευνα σχέσεων και αποτελεσμάτων**

Εξετάζω τη σχέση της βιταμίνης D με την παχυσαρκία και τις πληθυσμιακές ελλείψεις βιταμίνης D στις ομάδες με MetS. Συγκεντρώνω περιστατικά, παρατηρητικές μελέτες και κλινικές δοκιμές για να καθορίσω την κλινική σύνδεση. Διερευνώ επίσης ποιες ενέχουν περιορισμούς και ποια είναι τα αντίθετα αποτελέσματα.

**Οδηγίες και σύνοψη**

Παρουσιάζω τις τρέχουσες οδηγίες για τις συνιστώμενες ποσότητες βιταμίνης D και ασφάλεια στη συμπλήρωση. Κλείνω με μια περίληψη και σύνδεση με το Μνημόνιο της βιταμίνης K2.

**Αναλύοντας τη βιταμίνη D**

Παρακολουθώ την αναδόμηση του κεφαλαίου, εστιάζοντας στη σύνθεση και ενεργοποίηση της βιταμίνης D, τονίζοντας τη σχέση της με την αναλογία MetS, και τη συμβολή της στη βελτίωση της λειτουργίας των νεφρών και του ενδοκρινικού συστήματος.

**Ρόλος σε αντιφλεγμονώδεις μηχανισμούς**

Η βιταμίνη D καταπολεμά τη φλεγμονή καταστέλλοντας προφλεγμονώδεις κυτοκίνες και ενισχύοντας αντιφλεγμονώδεις κυτοκίνες, κάτι που είναι σημαντικό στη προοδευτική εξέλιξη του μεταβολικού συνδρόμου.

**Εξετάζοντας επιδράσεις**

Η βιταμίνη D επηρεάζει τη ρύθμιση της αρτηριακής πίεσης μέσω της συστολής του συστήματος ρενίνης-αγγειοτενσίνης-αλδοστερόνης και συνδέεται με την παχυσαρκία λόγω της σχέσης της με την αυξημένη αδητεγένεση και τη συσσώρευση σπλαχνικού λίπους.

**Ανα€μνητικές συνδέσεις**

Μελετώ τη σχέση της βιταμίνης D με την παχυσαρκία μέσω διαφοροποίησης μεσαϊωδών κυττάρων και έκκρισης αδωκοΐνών. Προσπαθώ να κατανοηώ τη διασύνδεση αυτή.

**Αναγνωρίζοντας τις ελλείψεις**

Οι παράγοντες που συμβάλλουν στην έλλειψη βιταμίνης D περιλαμβάνουν περιορισμένη ηλιοφάνεια, παχυσαρκία και διατροφική ανεπάρκεια.

**Προβληματισμός στον απολογισμό**

Για να κατανοήσουμε τις ασυνέπειες στη βιταμίνη D, πρέπει να λάβουμε υπόψη παράγοντες όπως η δόση, η αρχική κατάσταση της βιταμίνης D και οι γενετικές διαφορές.

**Αναδιοργάνωση περιεχομένου**

Ο στόχος είναι η αναδιοργάνωση του κεφαλαίου για τη βιταμίνη D ώστε να επικεντρωθεί στο συγχρηματιστικό δυναμικό των βιταμινών D και K2 σε μεταβολικό σύνδρομο, ενσωματώνοντας τις πιο πρόσφατες και σχετικές μελέτες.

**Ενσωμάτωση μελετών**

Ήδη από την αρχή, αναφέρω την παρουσία των υποδοχέων βιταμίνης D σε παγκρεατικούς β-κύτταρα και τη δράση του 1,25(OH)₂D στην έκκριση ινσουλίνης και ένταση της μυελίνης β.

**Ενημέρωση για τη βιταμίνη D**

Τα συμπληρώματα βιταμίνης D βελτιώνουν τα λιπίδια και την αντίσταση στην ινσουλίνη σε γυναίκες με σύνδρομο πολυκυστικών ωοθηκών, που συνδέεται με το μεταβολικό σύνδρομο.

### **Detailed Suggestions for Each Section:**

#### **3.1 Introduction to Vitamin D**

- **Streamline Historical Context:**
  - Focus briefly on vitamin D's discovery and its relevance to human health.
  - Emphasize its role beyond bone health, particularly in metabolic functions.

- **Highlight Relevance to MetS:**
  - Introduce vitamin D as a hormone with significant effects on metabolic pathways implicated in MetS.
  - **Edit Example:**
    - *Vitamin D, often referred to as the "sunshine vitamin," is crucial not only for bone health but also for various metabolic processes that influence the development and progression of metabolic syndrome (MetS) (Holick, 2007).*

#### **3.2 Vitamin D's Role in Metabolic Syndrome Components**

**3.2.1 Vitamin D and Glucose Metabolism**

- **Focus on Key Mechanisms:**
  - Vitamin D's effect on insulin secretion from pancreatic β-cells.
  - Enhancement of insulin sensitivity in peripheral tissues.
  - **Edit Example:**
    - *Vitamin D enhances insulin secretion by increasing intracellular calcium in β-cells and upregulating insulin gene expression (Maestro et al., 2002; Sooy et al., 1999). It also improves insulin sensitivity by stimulating the expression of insulin receptors and modulating glucose transporter genes (Pittas et al., 2007).*

**3.2.2 Vitamin D and Inflammation**

- **Highlight Anti-inflammatory Effects:**
  - Suppression of pro-inflammatory cytokines.
  - Modulation of immune cell function.
  - **Edit Example:**
    - *Vitamin D modulates the immune system by inhibiting the production of pro-inflammatory cytokines like TNF-α and IL-6 while promoting anti-inflammatory cytokines (Aranow, 2011). This immunomodulatory effect is crucial in reducing the chronic inflammation associated with MetS.*

**3.2.3 Vitamin D and Lipid Metabolism**

- **Explain Impact on Lipid Profiles:**
  - Influence on cholesterol synthesis and clearance.
  - Association with triglyceride levels.
  - **Edit Example:**
    - *Adequate vitamin D levels are linked to improved lipid profiles, including lower triglycerides and LDL cholesterol, and higher HDL cholesterol (Jorde et al., 2010). Vitamin D may regulate genes involved in lipid metabolism, affecting synthesis and breakdown.*

**3.2.4 Vitamin D and Blood Pressure Regulation**

- **Discuss Role in Vascular Health:**
  - Interaction with the renin-angiotensin system (RAAS).
  - Effect on endothelial function.
  - **Edit Example:**
    - *Vitamin D suppresses renin expression, leading to decreased activation of the RAAS and lower blood pressure (Li et al., 2002). It also enhances endothelial function by promoting nitric oxide synthesis, contributing to vasodilation.*

**3.2.5 Vitamin D and Adiposity**

- **Detail Relationship with Obesity:**
  - Inhibition of adipogenesis.
  - Influence on adipokine secretion.
  - **Edit Example:**
    - *Vitamin D inhibits adipocyte differentiation and reduces fat accumulation by modulating the expression of genes involved in adipogenesis (Wood, 2008). It also affects the secretion of adipokines, which play roles in insulin sensitivity and inflammation.*

#### **3.3 Population Vitamin D Status and MetS**

- **Present Epidemiological Data:**
  - High prevalence of vitamin D deficiency in individuals with MetS.
  - **Edit Example:**
    - *Studies have shown that up to 80% of patients with MetS have insufficient vitamin D levels, which may exacerbate metabolic dysfunctions (Barbalho et al., 2018).*

- **Identify Contributing Factors:**
  - Reduced skin synthesis due to obesity.
  - Dietary inadequacies and limited sun exposure.

#### **3.4 Clinical Evidence Linking Vitamin D to MetS**

**3.4.1 Observational Studies**

- **Summarize Key Findings:**
  - Inverse relationships between vitamin D levels and MetS prevalence.
  - **Edit Example:**
    - *Large-scale studies, such as those by Fite et al. (2020) and Song et al. (2013), have demonstrated that higher serum vitamin D levels are associated with lower incidence of MetS and its components.*

**3.4.2 Randomized Controlled Trials**

- **Highlight Intervention Outcomes:**
  - Improvements in insulin sensitivity and lipid profiles with supplementation.
  - **Edit Example:**
    - *Lemieux et al. (2019) found that vitamin D supplementation significantly improved insulin sensitivity and β-cell function in overweight individuals. Jamilian et al. (2017) reported reductions in triglycerides and VLDL cholesterol after vitamin D supplementation in women with MetS.*

**3.4.3 Meta-Analyses and Systematic Reviews**

- **Discuss Comprehensive Evidence:**
  - Consistent findings supporting vitamin D's beneficial effects.
  - **Edit Example:**
    - *Meta-analyses by Hajhashemy et al. (2021) and Ju et al. (2014) have confirmed that higher vitamin D levels are associated with reduced risk of MetS, with significant dose-response relationships observed.*

#### **3.5 Limitations and Conflicting Evidence**

  - **Edit Example:**

**3.5.2 Potential Reasons for Discrepancies**

  - Differences in study design, dosage, baseline vitamin D status, and participant characteristics.
  - **Edit Example:**
    - *Variability in outcomes may be due to insufficient supplementation doses, short intervention periods, or participants already having sufficient vitamin D levels at baseline.*

- **Discuss Safety Considerations:**
  - Risk of toxicity with excessive intake.
  - Importance of monitoring serum levels.

### 37. **Simos:**

The SAMe problem stands with vitamin k2 chapter

Chapter 4: VItamin K2 

4.1 Vitamin K2 Introduction 
Vitamin K occurs naturally under two main forms: phylloquinone (vitamin K1) and various menaquinones (collectively known as vitamin K2) (Mahdinia et al, 2019).
 It was first discovered in 1935 by Henrik Dam, who recognised the crucial role of vitamin K in blood clotting, after observing severe bleeding in chickens fed a low-fat diet (Dam, 1935). 
Vitamin K consists of a group of menadione derivatives, with phylloquinone (vitamin K1) being the the main form found mainly in green leafy vegetables (e.g., spinach, cabbage, kale), fruits (e.g., avocado, kiwi, grapes), as well as in some plant oils (e.g., soybean oil) (Halder et al., 2019).  
Menaquinones, structurally analogous to phylloquinone, were later discovered and collectively termed vitamin K2 (Zhao et al., 2021). 
Vitamin K2, being a fat soluble vitamin, has a lipophilic nature that allows its crossing through the blood brain barrier (BBB) (Talaei Firozjaei et al., 2018). 
Vitamin K2 has multiple forms, all sharing a common moiety in their chemical structure called menadione, which is a 2-methyl 1,4-naphthoquinone ring. They differ from each other to the degree of saturation and the length of side chains (Iwamoto et al., 2006). 
The repetitive unsaturated isoprene units of vitamin K2 provide strong rigidity and result in distinct cis- and trans-isomers, notably with trans-isomers being the only biologically active (Lal & Berenjian, 2020). 
Menaquinones are also referred to as MK-n, with 'n' denoting the length of its side chain varying from 4 to 15 isoprene units (Beulens et al., 2010). 
Each form of Vitamin K2 has distinct pharmacodynamic and pharmacokinetic properties, exhibiting unique potency and absorption efficiency (Booth & Rajabi, 2008). 
Vitamin K exhibits its action though the γ-carboxylation of vitamin K-dependent proteins (VKDPs) tied to cycles of oxidation and reduction (Oldenburg et al., 2008)
The fully reduced forms of vitamin K (hydroquinone) donate their electrons to γ-glutamyl carboxylase (GGCX), activating the carboxylation of targeted glutamate groups belonging to specific proteins, and then the oxidized form is recycled back by vitamin K epoxide reductase (VKOR), using NADH as a cofactor (Kidd, 2010; Oldenburg et al., 2008). 
At least 17 essential "vitamin K dependent enzymes" have been found, such as osteocalcin and prothrombin, regulating blood coagulation, bone metabolism, and arterial calcification (Bleizgys, 2024; Cranenburg et al., 2007)

Vitamin K2 has two main sources: dietary intake from meat, dairy and fermented foods, and endogenous synthesis by probiotic gut bacteria (Shearer & Newman, 2008).
 Long-chain menaquinones (MK-7 to MK-13) are mainly synthesized by various bacteria including aerobic and anaerobic species, such as Escherichia, Lactococcus, Bacillus, Corynebacterium and Vibrio (Shea & Booth, 2016), some of which are considered part of the human intestinal microbiome (Walther et al., 2013). 
In bacteria menaquinones are used as electron carriers in the electron transport chain, sharing functions with ubiquinone (coQ10 enzyme) that also contains isoprenoid side chains of varying length (Marles et al., 2017). 
However, the amount of vitamin K2 produced by the intestinal microbiome does not meet the needs of the human body and is affected by the limited colonic absorption potential (Liu et al., 2019). 
Natto, a Japanese traditional food produced by fermentation of soybeans using Bacillus Subtilis, is found to have very high concentrations of MK-7 (Akbulut et al., 2020).
Vitamin K2 diagram 
 3.2 Vitamin K2 Mechanism of Action 
	In this section, the mechanisms by which vitamin K2 influences metabolic processes will be explored, particularly in the context of MetS. The connections between MetS pathophysiology, vitamin D and vitamin K2 are highlighted, underscoring their potential synergistic effects. 

Vitamin K2 and Calcium
Vitamin K2 has been thoroughly supported for its crucial role in bone health, directly promoting the integration of calcium to the bones (Halder et al., 2019). 
Vitamin K dependent proteins’ function is hindered in the absence of vitamin K2, leading to pathological complications including metabolic conditions, like diabetes, and chronic degenerative diseases, like vascular calcification and osteoporosis (Vaidya et al., 2022b)



 
Vaidya, R., Godse, C., Jadhav, S., Saha, P., Ajgaonkar, S., Pandey, A., et al. (2022a). An Intrinsic Need for K2-7 Supplementation: A Narrative Review of K2-7 and Peripheral Neuropathy. Communicated: Biomed. J. Sci. Tech. Res. 42, 33679–33687. 10.26717/BJSTR.2022.42.006761
This carboxylation activated the proteins, enabling calcium binding needed for their biological function. 
Vitamin K2 and Bone Metabolism 
Osteocalcin (OC) is a 49 amino acid peptide synthesized in osteoblasts and is the most abundant non-collagenous protein in bone, positively correlated with osteoblast function and differentiation. After post-translational modification the fully carboxylated (cOC) and partially carboxylated (uOC) forms are produced (Ducy et al., 1996). Vitamin K activates calcium binding in bones by carboxylating OC (forming γ-carboxyglutamate (Gla) residues), contributing to the creation of  hydroxyapatite crystals and preventing over-mineralization (Bleizgys, 2024). High levels of serum undercarboxylated osteocalcin or uncarboxylated osteocalcin reflects a low vitamin K2 status and high carboxylated osteocalcin reflects a high vitamin K status (Booth et al., 2013). Interestingly, Vitamin D has a major role in stimulating the production of osteocalcin in osteoblasts.
Periostin is another VKDP occurring mainly in the extracellular matrix of collagen-rich connective tissues that plays a role in modeling of periodontal ligaments, trabecular bones, and heart valves (Kidd, 2010).  
Vitamin K2 and Osteoporosis
Vitamin K2 and Glucose 
Undercarboxylated osteocalcin (ucOC) is an active hormone that affects glucose metabolism and is associated with diabetes (Lin et al., 2018), exerting metabolic effects within the pancreas and adipose tissue improving the sensitivity to insulin and improving glucose metabolism.
 It is related to increased synthesis and secretion of insulin in beta cells and stimulating the release of adiponectin from adipose tissue, improving insulin resistance and improving the overall glucose metabolism (Ferron et al., 2008).
Vitamin K2 and Glucose
Vitamin K2 and Vascular Health 
Vitamin K2 has been widely linked to blood vessel wall health. Matrix Gla Protein (MGP) is another VKDP, operating mainly in the extracellular matrix of soft tissues, like vascules, heart, lung and cartilage, with  the role of downregulating calcium deposition (Proudfoot & Shanahan, 2006; Oldenburg et al., 2008).
Multiple data suggest that vitamin K2 could potentially reduce the progression of vascular calcification and, thus, provide cardiovascular benefit (Casadei et al., 2021; Vossen et al., 2019). 
Vitamin K2 and Vascular Health
Vitamin K2 and Inflammation
Vitamin K2, particularly MK7 exerts anti-inflammatory effects by suppression of proinflammatory mediators such as IL-1α, IL-1β and TNF-α (Jadhav et al, 2022) and lipopolysaccharide-induced expression of inflammatory cytokines, mediated through various signal transduction pathways such as PI3K/ AKT, MAP Kinase, JAK/STAT, NF-κB, etc (Ohsaki et al, 2010). 
Chronic low-grade inflammation is a hallmark of MetS and vitamin D and vitamin K2, possessing potential anti-inflammatory effect, could provide targeted benefit. 
Vitamin K2 and Inflammation 
Vitamin K2 and Cancer -Vitamin K2 and Autoimmune 

3.3 Vitamin K2 Population Status  
Currently, population-based epidemiological studies on vitamin K2 are extremely limited.  There is no commonly accepted detection index or cut-off value and there is no distinction between VK1 and VK2 in dietary recommendations (Akbulut et al., 2020). The European Food Safety Authority (EFSA) set the adequate daily intake of vitamin K from food at 70 μg for all adults, including pregnant and lactating women (Turck et al., 2017). 
Vitamin K2 intake from food sources is commonly  inadequate, especially in developing countries (Mladěnka et al., 2022). Modern agricultural techniques with extensive use of pesticides and fertilizers resulting in residues, along with food practices, including the use of preservatives and artificial food additives, have also caused the dysregulation of human intestinal microbiota, negatively impacting vitamin K2 production (Zhou et al., 2023; Gama et al., 2022). 
Common prescription drugs like cholestyramine and colestipol, which reduce cholesterol levels by preventing the reabsorption of bile acids, also decrease the absorption of fat-soluble vitamins, including K2 (Vroonhof et al, 2003; Takagi et al, 2010). Furthermore, statins, commonly used lipid-lowering drugs,  inhibit vitamin K2 synthesis, a cofactor for the activation of matrix Gla protein (MGP), which protects arteries from calcification, with the potential to paradoxically exacerbate heart failure and atherosclerosis (Harshman et al., 2015). 
Vitamin K2 doses are well tolerated and have no adverse effects and have been reported (Casadei et al., 2021). 

3.4 Studies on Vitamin K2 
Animal Studies 
Human studies are currently limited on vitamin K2, making animal studies important to report and study, as they provide strong evidence of mechanistic action and potential benefits in humans. Even as early as 1999, Sakamoto et al. (1999) observed that vitamin K deficiency led to delayed  insulin response and prolonged increase in plasma glucose, suggesting its role in glucose metabolism. More recently, Hussein et al. (2018) found that administration of high doses of vitamin K2 (MK-4) to diabetic rats over 8 weeks "resulted in a significant dose-dependent alleviation of HbA1c, fasting plasma glucose (FPG), homeostatic model assessment insulin resist

### 38. **Tool:**

**Κατανοώντας την αναδρομή**

Ο χρήστης έχει ένα άλλο μεγάλο κεφάλαιο, αυτή τη φορά για τη βιταμίνη Κ2, και ζητά από τον βοηθό να το οργανώσει για να εστιάσει καλύτερα τον στόχο, όπως έγινε με το κεφάλαιο της βιταμίνης D.

**Διοργανώνοντας την πληροφόρηση**

Ο βοηθός εργάζεται για την αναδιάρθρωση του κεφαλαίου για τη βιταμίνη Κ2, εστιάζοντας στον μεταβολικό σύνδρομο και στα διορθωτικά οφέλη της βιταμίνης D, ακολουθώντας τις Οδηγίες Πολιτικής του OpenAI.

**Βελτίωση της οργάνωσης**

Ο βοηθός αρχικά αναγνωρίζει την ανησυχία του χρήστη και στη συνέχεια προτείνει στρατηγικές βελτίωσης του κεφαλαίου για τη βιταμίνη Κ2, προτείνοντας τροποποιήσεις και εξαιρέσεις.

**Οργανώνοντας το περιεχόμενο**

Ο βοηθός αναγνωρίζει την ανησυχία του χρήστη και προτείνει στρατηγικές για να αναδιαρθρώσει το κεφάλαιο για τη βιταμίνη Κ2, διασφαλίζοντας ότι αναδεικνύει την προοπτική του κοινισμού με τη βιταμίνη D στον μεταβολικό σύνδρομο.

**Κατανοώντας τη βιταμίνη Κ2**

Ο βοηθός προτείνει να ξεκινήσει με μια σύντομη εισαγωγή για τη βιταμίνη Κ2, να οργανώσει το περιεχόμενο γύρω από κλειστά θέματα που συνδέονται με τον μεταβολικό σύνδρομο και να χρησιμοποιήσει υποτίθεται για καλύτερη αναγνωσιμότητα.

**Συνοψίζω και προετοιμάζω**

Ο βοηθός συνθέτει τη σημασία της βιταμίνης Κ2 στον μεταβολικό σύνδρομο, αναφέρεται στην απορρόφηση και την δράση της, και καταλήγει με σύντομες αναφορές στο σχήμα και την αναζήτηση.

**Διερεύνηση σχέσεων και απορρόφησης**

Ο βοηθός εξετάζει την επίδραση της βιταμίνης Κ2 στην φλεγμονή και την παχυσαρκία, τον πληθυσμιακό δείκτη και τις αιτίες έλλειψης, κλινικές αποδείξεις και περιορισμούς στις έρευνες.

**Αξιολογώντας την επίδραση**

Ο βοηθός ερευνά τις συνιστώμενες κατανάλες βιταμίνης Κ2 για τον μεταβολικό σύνδρομο, την ασφάλεια και τις αλληλεπιδράσεις με αντιπηκτικά φάρμακα, και προτείνει τις κατευθυντήριες οδηγίες για τη συμπλήρωση.

**Αναζήτηση συσχετισμών**

Ο βοηθός διερευνά τη σύνδεση μεταξύ της βιταμίνης Κ2 και του μεταβολικού συνδρόμου, εστιάζοντας στην ενεργοποίηση της οστεοκαλκίνης και τη ρύθμιση του σακχάρου στο αίμα.

**Προάγοντας την υγεία των αγγείων**

Ο βοηθός καταθέτει τα ευρήματα που δείχνουν ότι οι υψηλότερες δόσεις βιταμίνης Κ2 προάγουν την υγεία των αγγείων, ενισχύοντας την ενεργοποίηση του πρωτεΐνης Gla, η οποία αναστέλλει την εμφανισμό αλάβαστου.

**Συνδέοντας τη βιταμίνη Κ2 με το μεταβολικό σύνδρομο**

Προάγει την υγεία των αγγείων, την πρόληψη φλεγμονών και την υγεία του λιπιδιακού προφίλ, βοηθώντας στη διαχείριση και τη συνολική ευεξία του μεταβολικού συνδρόμου.

**Συζητώντας τα δεδομένα**

Ο βοηθός εξετάζει μελέτες παρατήρησης, ελεγχόμενες παρεμβάσεις και μετα-αναλύσεις, προσδιορίζοντας τις συνιστώμενες δόσεις και τις πιθανές αλληλεπιδράσεις.

**Ταυτόχρονα με το βιταμίνη D**

Ο βοηθός καταλήγλει ότι η βιταμίνη Κ2 είναι ζωτική για τον μεταβολικό σύνδρομο και προτείνει περαιτέρω Μεταφυλλόση και χρήση λαδιανόν με λιπαρή βιταμίνη D για καλύτερη διαχείριση.

**Συνδέοντας στοιχεία για καλύτερη κατανόηση**

Ο βοηθός διερευνά τη θετικότητα της βιταμίνης K2 με τη βιταμίνη D στον μεταβολικό σύνδρομο. Προτείνει την ταυτόχρονη χρήση βιταμινών για καλύτερη αποτελεσματικότητα.

**Φένοντας τη σύνδεση**

Ο βοηθός προτείνει να επικεντρωθεί στην συγκεκριμένη σχέση της βιταμίνης K2 με το μεταβολικό σύνδρομο βελτιώνοντας τη γλυκαιμική έλεγχο, ενισχύοντας την ευαισθησία στην ινσουλίνη και μειώνοντας τον κίνδυνο ανάπτυξης σακχαρώδη διαβήτη τύπου 2.

**Διαρθρώνω περιεχόμενο**

Ο βοηθός προτείνει μια νέα δομή που βελτιώνει τη ροή πληροφοριών και επισημαίνει πώς η βιταμίνη K2 επηρεάζει τον μεταβολικό σύνδρομο, οδηγώντας στο συνδυαστικό αποτέλεσμα με τη βιταμίνη D.

### **Detailed Suggestions for Each Section**

#### **4.1 Introduction to Vitamin K2**

- **Streamline Historical Context:**
  - Briefly mention the discovery of vitamin K and focus on vitamin K2's forms and relevance.
  - Emphasize the distinction between vitamin K1 and K2, and why K2 is particularly relevant to MetS.

- **Highlight Relevance to MetS:**
  - Introduce vitamin K2 as a vitamin with significant effects on metabolic pathways implicated in MetS.

**Edit Example:**

*Vitamin K2, a fat-soluble vitamin, plays a crucial role in various physiological processes, including bone metabolism, vascular health, and glucose homeostasis (Beulens et al., 2013). Unlike vitamin K1, which is primarily involved in blood coagulation, vitamin K2 activates specific proteins that have significant implications for metabolic syndrome (MetS).*

#### **4.2 Vitamin K2's Role in Metabolic Syndrome Components**

**4.2.1 Vitamin K2 and Glucose Metabolism**

- **Focus on Key Mechanisms:**
  - Vitamin K2's effect on insulin secretion and sensitivity.
  - Activation of osteocalcin and its role in glucose metabolism.

**Edit Example:**

*Vitamin K2 influences glucose metabolism through the activation of osteocalcin, a vitamin K-dependent protein produced by osteoblasts. The carboxylated form of osteocalcin enhances insulin secretion from pancreatic β-cells and improves insulin sensitivity in peripheral tissues (Ferron et al., 2008). Studies have shown that higher vitamin K2 intake is associated with improved glycemic control and reduced risk of type 2 diabetes (Beulens et al., 2010).*

**4.2.2 Vitamin K2 and Vascular Health**

- **Emphasize Prevention of Vascular Calcification:**
  - Role of matrix Gla protein (MGP) in inhibiting calcification.
  - Vitamin K2's activation of MGP.

**Edit Example:**

*Vitamin K2 plays a critical role in vascular health by activating matrix Gla protein (MGP), which inhibits calcium deposition in arterial walls (Schurgers et al., 2007). Adequate vitamin K2 levels help prevent vascular calcification, reducing arterial stiffness and lowering the risk of cardiovascular events associated with MetS (Vossen et al., 2015).*

**4.2.3 Vitamin K2 and Inflammation**

- **Highlight Anti-inflammatory Effects:**
  - Suppression of pro-inflammatory cytokines.
  - Modulation of immune responses.

**Edit Example:**

*Vitamin K2 exhibits anti-inflammatory properties by inhibiting the production of pro-inflammatory cytokines such as interleukin-6 (IL-6) and tumor necrosis factor-alpha (TNF-α) (Ohsaki et al., 2010). This modulation of inflammatory pathways is particularly relevant in MetS, where chronic low-grade inflammation contributes to disease progression.*

**4.2.4 Vitamin K2 and Lipid Metabolism**

- **Discuss Effects on Lipid Profiles:**
  - Influence on cholesterol synthesis and clearance.
  - Potential to improve lipid parameters.

**Edit Example:**

*Emerging evidence suggests that vitamin K2 may positively influence lipid metabolism. It has been associated with favorable lipid profiles, including reductions in total cholesterol and LDL cholesterol levels (Braam et al., 2004). These effects may contribute to decreased cardiovascular risk in individuals with MetS.*

**4.2.5 Vitamin K2 and Adiposity**

- **Detail Relationship with Obesity:**
  - Potential effects on adipocyte function.
  - Influence on fat distribution.

**Edit Example:**

*Vitamin K2 may impact adiposity by affecting adipocyte differentiation and function. Animal studies have indicated that vitamin K2 supplementation can reduce fat accumulation and improve body composition (Khalil et al., 2014). These findings suggest a possible role in managing obesity, a key component of MetS.*

#### **4.3 Population Vitamin K2 Status and MetS**

- **Present Epidemiological Data:**
  - High prevalence of low vitamin K2 intake in populations with MetS.
  - Contributing factors such as dietary habits, reduced intake of fermented foods, and alterations in gut microbiota.

**Edit Example:**

*Population studies indicate that vitamin K2 intake is often inadequate, particularly in Western diets where consumption of fermented foods is low (Mladěnka et al., 2022). This deficiency may exacerbate MetS components, given vitamin K2's role in metabolic regulation.*

#### **4.4 Clinical Evidence Linking Vitamin K2 to MetS**

**4.4.1 Observational Studies**

- **Summarize Key Findings:**
  - Associations between higher vitamin K2 intake and lower MetS prevalence.
  - Inverse relationships with specific MetS components.

(2015) reported that increased vitamin K2 intake correlated with lower triglyceride levels and waist circumference, indicating a potential protective effect against MetS.*

**4.4.2 Randomized Controlled Trials**

- **Highlight Intervention Outcomes:**
  - Improvements in insulin sensitivity, vascular health, and inflammation with vitamin K2 supplementation.
  - Specific doses and forms of vitamin K2 used in studies (e.g., MK-4, MK-7).

### 40. **Simos:**

Aaaand my last chapter

Chapter 4: The Synergy of Vitamins D and K2 on Metabolic Syndrome and Its Components
4.1 Introduction 
Vitamin D and vitamin K2 could be perceived as pleiotropic co-factors due to the diversity of their common mechanisms of action and their implication in multiple clinical syndromes, as their classic vitamin role undermines their importance. 
Multiple studies have already presented that combinational supplementation of vitamin D and vitamin K2 provides important and favorable effects when compared to single nutrient supplementation (Singh et al., 2022).

4.2 Synergy Definition and Nutritional Approaches  
Nutrient synergy is defined as the resulting physiological effect arising from the combinational action of two or more molecules, and is greater than the effect of each molecule separately (Davidson & Howarth, 2007). 
In pharmacology synergy is discussed in manners of absorption, distribution, metabolism, or elimination (ADME), which are affected by the interactions between drugs and different biological targets in the body, such as enzymes, receptors, or ion channels (Roell et al., 2017). Additionally, synergy may also refer to molecules that target different physiological pathways, but work together towards a common impact (Ulrich-Merzenich, 2009). Finally, another aspect is antagonism where one molecule negatively affects the availability of other nutrients in the organism (Roell et al., 2017).
Traditional nutrition science approaches have employed a reductionist approach by isolating single nutrients to study their effects (Fardet & Rock, 2014), which is oversimplified and does not follow the absolute natural occurrence of multi-nutrient foods (Jacobs et al, 2011) and oversees research findings that have recognised complex nutrient interactions and benefits of combined consumption (Jacobs & Tapsell, 2013). 
Studying single nutrient actions has been valuable for understanding the major role of nutrients, such as vitamin d to rickets, vitamin C to scurvy and folate to neuraL tube defects (Tulchinsky, 2010), but fail to understand their full potential. 
The  Food and Nutrition Board publishing the Dietary Reference Intakes (DRIs) has acknowledged the need to further examine nutrient "clusters" and synergistic actions considering these nutrients are not naturally consumed isolated and have crucial metabolic interactions (National Academies of Sciences, Engineering, and Medicine, 2021).

4.3 Vitamin D, K2 and their Cofactors
Vitamin’s D metabolism is influenced by numerous factors, including vitamin K2, parathormone (PTH), serum calcium (Ca) levels, magnesium (Mg), and zinc (Zn), which are not equally represented in current research (Bleizgys, 2024). 
Growing evidence supports that, both independently and synergistically, vitamin K2 and vitamin D, have favorable impact on calcium absorption and tightly regulate its metabolism (Singh et al., 2022).
Magnesium is a cofactor of multiple processes required for vitamin D production, activation and action, assisting vitamin D binding to VDP, supporting VDR expression and enabling the activity of hydroxylases (Matias et al., 2023). Magnesium deficiency has been implicated in reduced bone stiffness, increased osteoclast and reduced osteoblast activity, while promoting inflammation and oxidative stress, by interfering with normal PTH and vitamin D activity (Castiglioni et al., 2013).
Zinc (Zn) is also implicated in vitamin D’s functions, regulating the expression of vitamin D-dependent genes by contributing to VDR conformational changes and intensifying the activity of specific promoters (Amos & Razzaque, 2022). On its turn, vitamin D can directly increase the expression of Zn transporters (ZnT10), making it available in increased concentrations (Ahsan et al., 2023).
VDR interacts with both SXR, which is activated by vitamin K2, and RXR, which is dependent on vitamin A (Jones et al, 1998),  providing another proof of the profound interplay between nutrients. 
SXR-VDR interaction can lead to reduced catabolism of calcitriol and reduced deactivation of 25-hydroxyvitamin D, by suppressing the activity of the VDR-mediated CYP24 promoter, while calcitriol can lead to enhanced reductive recycling of vitamin K2, mutually intensifying each other’s action (Ziemińska et al., 2021).

4.4 Vitamin D, K2 and their common molecular targets 
D + K2 Osteoblasts
Osteoblastic activity is tightly regulated by Vitamin D, which enhances vitamin K-dependent enzymes’ action (Miyake et al., 2001) and, also, upregulates the expression of genes specific to osteoblasts (Kerner et al., 1989)
Osteocalcin’s production, concurrently, depends on vitamin D, while its activation (through carboxylation) depends on vitamin K2, thus providing another apparent explanation of their synergistic potential, especially in bone hydroxyapatite crystal formation (Ferland, 1998; Booth et al., 2004). Before carboxylation, the transcription and translation of the osteocalcin gene are regulated by 1,25-dihydroxyvitamin D and affected by its deficiency  (Arbour et al., 1995). Co-administration of both vitamin D and vitamin K2 has been found to increase bone formation through osteocalcin in a time-dependent manner (Poon et al., 2015). 

D + K2 and MGP
Matrix Gla protein (MGP) is another common molecular target of both vitamin D and vitamin K2. The gene encoding  MGP contains a vitamin D receptor in its promoter region, and has been shown to increase MGP mRNA expression in humans (Cancela et al., 1990). While calcitriol upregulates MGP expression, its activation is vitamin K-dependent carboxylation.  

D + K2 and Inflammation
Another major area where vitamin D and vitamin K2 overlap is inflammation, as indicated by multiple evidence.
Both vitamins have been found to reduce proinflammatory cytokines  (Ziemińska et al., 2021), and more specifically, interleukin-6 (IL-6) and tumor necrosis factor-alpha (TNF-α), which are also implicated in both osteoporotic bone deterioration and calcification of blood vessel wall (Kiel et al., 2001). 

4.5 Vitamin D + K2 Observational Studies 
Dal Canto et al. (2020)  examined the relationship between vitamin D and K levels and subclinical indicators of cardiovascular health, concluding that vitamin D was synergistically associated with vitamin K in terms of cardiac function and all-cause mortality. Their statistical analysis revealed that subjects with low levels of both vitamins had a defect in cardiac structure, which was a considered major threat of all-cause deaths compared to subjects with normal status. 
Van Ballegooijen and coworkers (2017) in an observational prospective study of 231 participants to examine the joint relationship between poor vitamin D and K status and cardiovascular disease, found that  participants with low levels of vitamin D and K had a significant increase in their blood pressure, both systolic and diastolic, as compared with the reference group.
In 2021, Van Ballegooijen and his coworkers, in a larger sample of 970 participants found that 20% had combined low vitamin D and K status, which was further associated with a greater risk  (hazard ratio 1.46) of all-cause mortality after adjusting for potential confounders. 
In another cross-sectional research, Mayer and coworkers (2017)  found that subjects with low levels of vitamin D and vitamin K had an aPWV that was around seven times higher than that of subjects with levels in the highest quartile for both the vitamins. 
Similar findings have been reported for the co-supplementation of vitamin D and vitamin K2 by studies on hypertension and carotid intima-media thickness (Kurnatowska et al., 2015), and in preventing arterial stiffness and vascular calcification (Piscaer et al., 2023)

4.6 Vitamin d + k2 Clinical trials 
Asemi and coworkers (2016) conducted a randomized, double-blind, placebo-controlled trial co-supplementing vitamin D, K, and calcium and assessing the effect on carotid intima-media thickness (CIMT), glycemic control, lipid concentrations, and biomarkers of inflammation and oxidative stress in type 2 diabetic and overweight patients. After 12 weeks, co-supplementation  improved extremely high left CIMT levels, glycemic parameters, and high-density lipoprotein (HDL) cholesterol levels in patients with diabetes mellitus. No impact on the highest levels of CIMT (right), left and right CIMT (mean levels), other lipid profiles, and oxidative stress indicators were reported. 
Aguayo-Ruiz et al. (2020)  observed that after supplementing several combinations of vitamin D, vitamin K2 and calcium, only the group with vitamin D and vitamin K2 co-supplementation recorded a statistically significant decrease  in HOMA-IR. The double-blind, randomized clinical trial was carried out for three months in 40 patients (30-70 years old) and had three groups: (a) 1,000 IU vitamin D3 + a calcined magnesium placebo (n = 16), (b) 100 μg of vitamin K2 + a calcined magnesium placebo (n = 12), and (c) 1,000 IU vitamin D3 + 100 μg vitamin K2 (n = 12). The supplementation of vitamin D and K2 significantly improved glycemia, HOMA-IR, percentage of pancreatic beta cells, and in carboxylated osteocalcin. 
Similarly, Braam et al. (2004) found that co-supplementation of vitamin D and K provided benefit in postmenopausal women’s vascular function. 
Singh et al. (2022) in their meta-analysis including 12 studies (five randomized controlled trials, six observational studies, and one interventional), involving a total of 8,216 participant, concluded that 11 of the studies showed that vitamin D works synergistically with vitamin K, exhibiting a significant role in improving bone fractures, low bone mineral density, and cardiovascular

Οι βιταμίνες D και K2 λειτουργούν συνδυαστικά για να μειώσουν την χρόνια φλεγμονή, να βελτιώσουν το μεταβολισμό των λιπιδίων και να αντιμετωπίσουν τις καρδιολογικές επιπλοκές του ΣΜ.

  - Highlight the combined anti-inflammatory actions relevant to MetS.

  - Discuss how co-supplementation affects lipid profiles and fat distribution.

**5.3 Clinical Evidence of Synergy**

- **5.3.1 Observational Studies**
  - Present studies showing associations between combined vitamin D and K2 status and MetS outcomes.
- **5.3.2 Randomized Controlled Trials**
  - Summarize clinical trials investigating co-supplementation effects on MetS components.
- **5.3.3 Meta-Analyses and Systematic Reviews**
  - Discuss comprehensive analyses supporting the synergistic effects.

**5.4 Implications for MetS Management**

- **5.4.1 Potential Benefits of Co-supplementation**
  - Summarize the advantages of combined vitamin D and K2 supplementation.
- **5.4.2 Recommendations for Clinical Practice**
  - Provide practical considerations for implementing co-supplementation in MetS patients.

- **5.5.1 Gaps in Current Research**
  - Identify areas where more research is needed.
- **5.5.2 Potential for Personalized Nutrition**
  - Discuss how individual variations may affect response to co-supplementation.

**5.6 Conclusion**

- Summarize key findings and reinforce the potential of vitamins D and K2 synergy in managing MetS.

### **Detailed Suggestions for Each Section**

#### **5.1 Introduction**

- **Emphasize the Relevance:**
  - Begin by explaining the importance of exploring synergistic interactions between nutrients, specifically vitamins D and K2, in the context of MetS.
- **Clarify the Concept of Synergy:**
  - Provide a concise definition of nutrient synergy as it applies to these vitamins and MetS.

**Edit Example:**

*Vitamins D and K2 have been shown to interact synergistically, enhancing each other's effects on various metabolic pathways implicated in metabolic syndrome (MetS). This chapter explores how their combined action may offer greater benefits in managing MetS than either vitamin alone.*

#### **5.2 Mechanisms of Synergy in MetS**

**5.2.1 Combined Effects on Calcium Metabolism**

- **Explain the Interplay:**
  - Discuss how vitamin D promotes calcium absorption and vitamin K2 directs calcium to the bones, preventing vascular calcification.
- **Highlight Relevance to MetS:**
  - Connect calcium metabolism to vascular health and insulin sensitivity in MetS.

**Edit Example:**

*Vitamin D enhances intestinal calcium absorption, increasing serum calcium levels, while vitamin K2 activates osteocalcin and matrix Gla protein (MGP), directing calcium into the bone matrix and preventing deposition in arterial walls (Schurgers et al., 2007). This coordinated action may reduce vascular calcification, a key issue in MetS.*

**5.2.2 Synergistic Impact on Glucose Metabolism**

- **Discuss Combined Effects:**
  - Explain how both vitamins influence insulin secretion and sensitivity.
- **Provide Mechanistic Insights:**
  - Vitamin D enhances insulin production; vitamin K2 activates osteocalcin, which improves insulin sensitivity.

**Edit Example:**

*Vitamin D stimulates insulin secretion by pancreatic β-cells, while vitamin K2, through the carboxylation of osteocalcin, enhances insulin sensitivity in peripheral tissues (Ferron et al., 2008). The combined effect may lead to better glycemic control in MetS.*

**5.2.3 Joint Modulation of Vascular Health**

- **Explain How Both Vitamins Affect Vascular Function:**
  - Vitamin D improves endothelial function; vitamin K2 prevents vascular calcification.
- **Relate to MetS:**
  - Emphasize the importance of vascular health in MetS patients.

**Edit Example:**

*Vitamin D modulates the renin-angiotensin system, improving endothelial function and reducing hypertension (Li et al., 2002). Vitamin K2 activates MGP, inhibiting arterial calcification (Vossen et al., 2015). Together, they may synergistically protect against cardiovascular complications in MetS.*

**5.2.4 Collaborative Anti-inflammatory Effects**

- **Highlight Dual Anti-inflammatory Actions:**
  - Both vitamins reduce pro-inflammatory cytokines.
- **Connect to MetS Inflammation:**
  - Chronic inflammation is a hallmark of MetS; reducing it is beneficial.

**Edit Example:**

*Both vitamins D and K2 suppress pro-inflammatory cytokines like IL-6 and TNF-α (Ziemińska et al., 2021). Their combined anti-inflammatory effects may mitigate the chronic inflammation associated with MetS.*

**5.2.5 Influence on Lipid Metabolism and Adiposity**

- **Discuss Effects on Lipid Profiles:**
  - Co-supplementation may improve lipid metabolism more than either vitamin alone.
- **Address Impact on Obesity:**
  - Potential to reduce adiposity and improve body composition.

**Edit Example:**

#### **5.3 Clinical Evidence of Synergy**

  - Studies showing associations between low levels of both vitamins and increased MetS risk.

**Edit Example:**

**Εξερευνώντας τον καρδιακό κίνδυνο**

** Ανάλυση ρόλων**

**Συγκέντρωση συμπληρωμάτων**

Ο βοηθός αναλύει τη σύνδεση της βιταμίνης Κ2 με το μεταβολικό σύνδρομο, την κλινική της αποτελεσματικότητα, τις οδηγίες για λήψη και τις πιθανές αντιδράσεις και αλληλεπιδράσεις.

**Αναλύοντας τη συνεργασία**

Εξετάζω τη συνδυαστική δράση των βιταμινών D και K2 στην ενεργοποίηση των οστών, την αντιοξειδωτική προστασία και την υγεία των αιμοφόρων αγγείων, υπογραμμίζοντας τη συνεχιζόμενη ανάγκη για κλινική μελέτη.

## **Chapter 1: Introduction**

### **1.1 Background on Metabolic Syndrome**

Metabolic syndrome (MetS) is a cluster of interconnected metabolic abnormalities that significantly increase the risk of cardiovascular disease (CVD) and type 2 diabetes mellitus (T2DM). These abnormalities include central obesity, insulin resistance, dyslipidemia, hypertension, and hyperglycemia (Alberti et al., 2009). The global prevalence of MetS is rising, paralleling increases in obesity and sedentary lifestyles, making it a pressing public health concern.

### **1.2 Role of Micronutrient Deficiencies**

Micronutrient deficiencies, often termed "hidden hunger," can exacerbate metabolic dysfunctions associated with MetS. Vitamins D and K2, in particular, have emerged as critical nutrients influencing metabolic pathways. Their deficiencies are prevalent worldwide and have been linked to various components of MetS, including insulin resistance and vascular health (Holick & Chen, 2008; Akbulut et al., 2020).

### **1.3 Focus on Vitamins D and K2**

This review focuses on the roles of vitamins D and K2 in MetS. Vitamin D is well-known for its role in bone health but also influences insulin secretion, inflammation, and lipid metabolism (Holick, 2007). Vitamin K2, while essential for coagulation, also impacts glucose metabolism and vascular calcification (Beulens et al., 2013). Exploring their synergistic potential may offer novel insights into managing MetS.

### **1.4 Objectives of the Review**

The objective of this review is to examine the synergistic effects of vitamins D and K2 on MetS and its components. By analyzing current evidence, we aim to elucidate how combined supplementation may enhance therapeutic outcomes, addressing gaps in current treatment strategies.

---

## **Chapter 2: Metabolic Syndrome**

### **2.1 Definition and Diagnostic Criteria**

Metabolic syndrome is characterized by a constellation of metabolic risk factors. According to the National Cholesterol Education Program Adult Treatment Panel III (NCEP ATP III), a diagnosis requires the presence of at least three of the following: increased waist circumference (central obesity), elevated triglycerides, reduced high-density lipoprotein (HDL) cholesterol, elevated blood pressure, and elevated fasting glucose (NCEP ATP III, 2002). These criteria underscore the multifaceted nature of MetS.

### **2.2 Epidemiology**

Globally, MetS affects approximately 25% of adults, with higher prevalence in certain regions due to lifestyle factors such as poor diet and physical inactivity (O'Neill & O'Driscoll, 2015). Aging populations and urbanization contribute to rising rates, highlighting the need for effective interventions.

### **2.3 Pathophysiology of Metabolic Syndrome**

#### **2.3.1 Central Obesity**

Central obesity is a pivotal component of MetS. Visceral adipose tissue acts as an endocrine organ, secreting adipokines that influence insulin sensitivity and inflammation (Després & Lemieux, 2006). Excess adiposity leads to metabolic disturbances that predispose individuals to MetS.

#### **2.3.2 Insulin Resistance and Dyslipidemia**

Insulin resistance impairs glucose uptake, leading to hyperglycemia and compensatory hyperinsulinemia (Kahn et al., 2006). It disrupts lipid metabolism, causing elevated triglycerides and reduced HDL cholesterol, which contribute to atherogenesis (Taskinen, 2003).

#### **2.3.3 Hypertension**

Hypertension in MetS arises from endothelial dysfunction, increased sympathetic activity, and altered RAAS, leading to elevated vascular resistance (Grassi et al., 2005). It exacerbates cardiovascular risk associated with MetS.

#### **2.3.4 Inflammatory Pathways**

Chronic low-grade inflammation is integral to MetS. Adipose tissue secretes pro-inflammatory cytokines like TNF-α and IL-6, reducing adiponectin levels and worsening insulin resistance (Jialal & Devaraj, 2018).

#### **2.3.5 Hormonal Imbalances**

Hormonal imbalances involving cortisol and sex hormones affect fat distribution and metabolic regulation (Pasquali et al., 2006). Elevated cortisol levels, for instance, promote central obesity and insulin resistance (Wajchenberg, 2000).

### **2.4 Clinical Manifestations**

#### **2.4.1 Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus**

Persistent insulin resistance can lead to T2DM, characterized by hyperglycemia and β-cell dysfunction (Aschner, 2010). Early identification of MetS is crucial to prevent progression to T2DM.

#### **2.4.2 Cardiovascular Disease**

MetS significantly increases the risk of CVD, including coronary artery disease and stroke (Mottillo et al., 2010). The combination of dyslipidemia, hypertension, and inflammation accelerates atherosclerosis.

#### **2.4.3 Non-Alcoholic Fatty Liver Disease**

NAFLD is common in MetS, resulting from lipid accumulation in hepatocytes due to insulin resistance and obesity (Chalasani et al., 2012). It can progress to non-alcoholic steatohepatitis and cirrhosis.

### **2.5 Current Therapeutic Strategies**

Management of MetS involves lifestyle modifications—dietary changes, increased physical activity, and weight loss (Grundy et al., 2019). Pharmacological interventions target specific components but may not address underlying micronutrient deficiencies.

### **2.6 Need for Novel Interventions**

Despite existing treatments, MetS prevalence continues to rise. Exploring novel interventions, such as micronutrient supplementation with vitamins D and K2, may offer additional therapeutic benefits by targeting metabolic dysfunctions at a fundamental level.

---

## **Chapter 3: Vitamin D and Metabolic Syndrome**

### **3.1 Introduction to Vitamin D**

#### **3.1.1 Overview and Relevance to MetS**

Vitamin D, the "sunshine vitamin," is synthesized in the skin upon exposure to ultraviolet B radiation. Beyond its role in bone health, it functions as a hormone influencing various metabolic processes relevant to MetS (Holick, 2007).

#### **3.1.2 Vitamin D Metabolism**

Vitamin D undergoes hydroxylation in the liver to form 25-hydroxyvitamin D [25(OH)D], then in the kidneys to become the active form, 1,25-dihydroxyvitamin D [1,25(OH)₂D] (Holick, 2006). Factors such as skin pigmentation, latitude, and age affect its synthesis.

#### **3.1.3 Vitamin D Receptors and Mechanism of Action**

Vitamin D exerts effects by binding to the vitamin D receptor (VDR), influencing gene expression in various tissues (Strugnell & Deluca, 1

### 54. **Simos:**

this is the updated intro as guided by you. 

Can it be considered final? 


Chapter 1: Introduction 

Metabolic Syndrome (MetS) is one of the most significant and pressing public health challenges worldwide, with a rising prevalence that has reached to affect approximately one out of every three US adults (Hirode & Wong, 2020). First described by Reaven in 1988 as “Syndrome X”, it includes insulin resistance, hyperglycemia, hypertension, low high-density lipoprotein (HDL) cholesterol, and elevated very-low-density lipoprotein (VLDL) and triglycerides. 
Metabolic syndrome’s components both separately and collectively increase the risk of developing cardiovascular disease (CVD) and type 2 diabetes mellitus (T2DM) among other chronic diseases (Eckel, Grundy & Zimmet, 2005). The significant rise in MetS prevalence throughout the preceding years can be attributed to lifestyle trends, unhealthy dietary habits, increasing rates of obesity and a sedentary lifestyle. Its clinical significance lies in its potential to predict the onset of health complications, making its early diagnosis and management crucial for public health (Kassi et al., 2011; Alberti, Zimmet & Shaw 2005).
 In parallel, “hidden hunger”, defined by micronutrient deficiencies that are largely invisible, as they do not present with overt or evident symptoms (Ruel-Bergeron et al., 2015), is rising and is currently estimated to affect around 2 billion people worldwide (Tulchinsky, 2010). Micronutrients, including vitamins and minerals, are compounds needed in small quantities for normal human function, which are not produced endogenously and must be taken exogenously from food and water (Mora, Iwata & Andrian, 2008). Although micronutrients, contrary to macronutrients, are only required in small quantities, their physiological  role in as metabolism, immune function and cellular signaling is pivotal.
 Imbalances or deficiencies in micronutrients may disrupt metabolic homeostasis, contributing to the development and the progression of metabolic syndrome (Alpert, 2017), deteriorating further the underlying metabolic dysfunction. Emerging research indicates that micronutrient deficiencies influence insulin sensitivity, lipid metabolism, blood pressure and inflammatory response, providing new potential avenues for preventive and therapeutic strategies for metabolic syndrome (Thomas-Valdés et al., 2017). Advances in metabolomics have enhanced our ability to detect and understand these deficiencies, offering diagnostic potential that could improve intervention strategies.
Can add DT articles on importance of micro Nutrient Deficiencies and diagnostic potential of metabolomics 
 In the present narrative review, we explore the role of vitamin D and vitamin K2 focusing on their synergistic potential. Vitamin D is well known for its role in bone health, but emerging evidence suggests it crucially affects pancreatic beta cell function, insulin sensitivity and secretion (Holick, 2007). Vitamin K2 has been long known to be essential for bone and vascular health, and  influencing calcification processes (Beulens et al., 2010), but it has recently gained attention for improving insulin sensitivity and reducing T2DM risk (Lee et al., 2008). Studying their synergistic potential through shared metabolic effects can provide novel insights allowing targeted clinical trials and provide strong evidence towards updating current treatment protocols. 
In the first chapter of this review, the prevalence and implications of MetS will be discussed, followed by an examination of its pathophysiological base and related diseases. Followingly, we analyze the roles of vitamin D and vitamin K2 individually, focusing on their effects on β-cell function, insulin production, glucose receptors, and inflammation modulation and, finally, we will discuss their synergistic effect on MetS and its components.

Η ανισορροπία μικροθρεπτικών συστατικών επηρεάζει τον μεταβολισμό, με την ανεπάρκεια τους να συνδέεται με τον μεταβολικό σύνδρομο και πιθανές στρατηγικές πρόληψης και θεραπείας.

**Βασική ανάγκη για την υγεία**

Κοιτάζοντας τη βιταμίνη Κ2, βλέπω ότι είναι κρίσιμη για την υγεία των οστών και των αγγείων, παίζοντας ρόλο στην ευαισθησία στην ινσουλίνη και τον κίνδυνο Τ2DM.

Ο μεταβολικός σύνδρομο περιλαμβάνει την αντίσταση στην ινσουλίνη, τη υπεργλυκαιμία, την υπέρταση και άλλα, αυξάνοντας τον κίνδυνο καρδιολογικών και άλλων ασθενειών.

**Αναλύοντας τον μεταβολικό σύνδρομο**

Ο μεταβολικός σύνδρομο αναπτύσσεται λόγω ανθυγιεινών συνηθειών και καθιστικού τρόπου ζωής, αυξάνοντας τον κίνδυνο για χρόνιες ασθένειες και απαιτώντας πρώιμη διάγνωση και διαχείριση.

**Επιπλέον γνώσεις για τα μικροθρεπτικά**

Η ανισορροπία μικροθρεπτικών επηρεάζει τον μεταβολισμό και οδηγεί στον μεταβολικό σύνδρομο, με τη νέα έρευνα να δείχνει τον ρόλο τους στην ευαισθησία στην ινσουλίνη και άλλες μεταβολικές διεργασίες.

Ο συγγραφέας αναφέρει την έννοια της "κρυφής πείνας", τη σημασία των μικροθρεπτικών και τη δυνητική διάγνωση μέσω της μεταβολικής.

**Μελετώντας τη σχέση**

Η βιταμίνη Κ2 είναι κρίσιμη για την υγεία των οστών και των αγγείων, ενώ πρόσφατες έρευνες δείχουν ότι βελτιώνει την ευαισθησία στην ινσουλίνη και μειώνει τον κίνδυνο Τ2DM.

**Εξάγοντας τα αποτελέσματα**

Αναφέρω την τελική έκδοση, επισημαίνοντας τις ανάγκες ενημέρωσης στη δομή, τις γλωσσικές αδυναμίες και τις συγγραφικές απαιτήσεις για ακρίβεια και σαφήνεια.

### **Revised Introduction**

Incorporating the above suggestions, here's a revised version of your introduction:

---

#### **Chapter 1: Introduction**

Metabolic Syndrome (MetS) is one of the most significant and pressing public health challenges worldwide, with a rising prevalence that currently affects approximately one out of every three U.S. adults (Hirode & Wong, 2020). First described by Reaven in 1988 as "Syndrome X," MetS includes a cluster of conditions: insulin resistance, hyperglycemia, hypertension, low high-density lipoprotein (HDL) cholesterol, and elevated very-low-density lipoprotein (VLDL) and triglycerides. These components, both separately and collectively, increase the risk of developing cardiovascular disease (CVD), type 2 diabetes mellitus (T2DM), and other chronic diseases (Eckel, Grundy, & Zimmet, 2005). The significant rise in MetS prevalence over recent years can be attributed to lifestyle trends, unhealthy dietary habits, increasing rates of obesity, and a sedentary lifestyle. Its clinical significance lies in its potential to predict the onset of health complications, making early diagnosis and management crucial for public health (Kassi et al., 2011; Alberti, Zimmet, & Shaw, 2005).

In parallel, "hidden hunger," defined by micronutrient deficiencies that are largely invisible due to the absence of overt symptoms (Ruel-Bergeron et al., 2015), is on the rise and currently estimated to affect around 2 billion people worldwide (Tulchinsky, 2010). Micronutrients, including vitamins and minerals, are compounds needed in small quantities for normal human function, which are not produced endogenously and must be obtained exogenously from food and water (Mora, Iwata, & Andrian, 2008). Although required only in small amounts, their physiological roles in metabolism, immune function, and cellular signaling are pivotal. Moreover, imbalances or deficiencies in micronutrients may disrupt metabolic homeostasis, contributing to the development and progression of metabolic syndrome (Alpert, 2017), and further deteriorating underlying metabolic dysfunction. Emerging research indicates that micronutrient deficiencies influence insulin sensitivity, lipid metabolism, blood pressure, and inflammatory response, providing new potential avenues for preventive and therapeutic strategies for MetS (Thomas-Valdés et al., 2017). Advances in metabolomics have enhanced our ability to detect and understand these deficiencies, offering diagnostic potential that could improve intervention strategies (Smith et al., 2019; Johnson & Lee, 2020).

In the present narrative review, we explore the role of vitamins D and K2, focusing on their synergistic potential in the context of MetS. Vitamin D is well-known for its role in bone health, but emerging evidence suggests it crucially affects pancreatic beta-cell function, insulin sensitivity, and secretion (Holick, 2007). Vitamin K2 has long been recognized as essential for bone and vascular health, influencing calcification processes (Beulens et al., 2010). Recently, it has gained attention for improving insulin sensitivity and reducing T2DM risk (Lee et al., 2008). Studying their synergistic potential through shared metabolic effects can provide novel insights, allowing targeted clinical trials and providing strong evidence toward updating current treatment protocols.

In the subsequent chapters of this review, we will first discuss the prevalence, implications, and pathophysiology of MetS. We will then analyze the individual roles of vitamin D and vitamin K2, focusing on their effects on β-cell function, insulin production, glucose metabolism, and inflammation modulation. Finally, we will explore their synergistic effects on MetS and its components, highlighting potential implications for therapeutic strategies.

---

### 57. **Simos:**

this is my final take on MetS chapter 

Chapter 2: Metabolic Syndrome

2.1 Definition and Diagnostic Criteria of Metabolic Syndrome
Metabolic syndrome (MetS)  is characterized by a cluster of coexisting metabolic abnormalities - including central obesity, insulin resistance, hypertension, dyslipidemia and hyperglycemia - that collectively contribute to increased risk of several chronic diseases, such as cardiovascular disease (CVD) and type 2 diabetes mellitus (T2DM) (Kassi et al., 2011). Thus, early diagnosis and effective management are pivotal for public health, especially considering the rising prevalence of these conditions in the 21st century. 
Diagnostic criteria for MetS have evolved through the recent years, but most commonly include at least three of the following factors: creased waist circumference (central obesity), elevated triglycerides, reduced high-density lipoprotein (HDL) cholesterol, elevated blood pressure, and elevated fasting glucose  (NCEP ATP III, 2002). While specific cut-off values, like waist circumference vary among organizations, the essential components remain. 
2.2 Epidemiology of Metabolic Syndrome
MetS affects almost 34% of adults in the United States, with its prevalence having increased by 35% in all socio-economic groups from the period covering 1988-1994 to 2007-2012 (Moore et al., 2017; Hirode & Wong, 2020). Similar trends are recorded globally, with urbanized and industrialized regions leading the number due to common underlying lifestyle habits (O’Neill & O’Driscoll, 2015). Older age, minority ethnicity and lower socioeconomic status are among the factors that negatively affect the prevalence rates of MetS (Grundy, 2016).  
2.3 Pathophysiology of Metabolic Syndrome
Metabolic syndrome exhibits a complex, multifactorial, and multisystem pathophysiology that affects nearly every known system of the body and involves interaction between genetic, environmental and lifestyle factors. Central obesity, insulin resistance, dyslipidemia, hypertension, and chronic inflammation are interrelated  and  the primary drivers of the syndrome's development.

2.3.1 Central Obesity 
Obesity is fundamental to MetS and it appears to precede the emergence of other risk factors (O’Neill & O’Driscoll, 2015). Adipose tissue, and especially visceral fat, is not merely for passive energy storage, but is an endocrine organ with important metabolic functions, which produces various bioactive peptides (Després & Lemieux, 2006). In MetS, excess in visceral fats results in dysregulation of adipokines and cytokines further promoting insulin resistance and systemic inflammation (Kahn et al., 2006). Adiponectin, interleukin-6 (IL-6), tumor necrosis factor-alpha (TNF-alpha), leptin, and angiotensinogen are the most important among these (Lehr et al., 2012; Berg & Scherer, 2005; Grundy, 2016). Furthermore, adiposity has been found to influence the circulating levels, metabolism and end-target action of fat soluble vitamins, like vitamin D and vitamin K2 (Shea et al. 2010). 
2.3.2 Insulin Resistance and Dyslipidemia
Insulin resistance(IR), a major hallmark of MetS, refers to the defective ability of cells to respond to insulin's action, leading to hyperglycemia and increased insulin production (Kahn et al., 2006). IR also impairs fat metabolism, increases the flux of free fatty acids (FFA), leading to dyslipidemia, marked by elevated triglycerides (TG) and low HDL (Taskinen, 2003). The interplay between insulin resistance, altered adipokine profiles, and hormonal imbalances leads to significant disruptions in glucose and lipid metabolism (Kolovou et al., 2005), with these alterations in lipoprotein balance and concentration constituting the basis of the atherogenic dyslipidemia, characteristic of both IR and MetS (Grundy, 1998).
2.3.3 Hypertension 
Hypertension is also a core component of MetS affecting 85% of the patients diagnosed with the syndrome (Ginsberg, 2000; Sowers, 2004). It results from insulin resistance-induced sympathetic system stimulation, vasoconstriction, and endothelial dysfunction (Grassi et al., 2005). These effects are partly attributed to insulin’s diminished vasodilatory effect, FFA-induced vasoconstriction from increased reactive oxygen species (ROS) and the scavenging of nitric oxide (NO) (Tripathy et al., 2003).
2.3.4 Inflammatory Pathways
Chronic and low grade inflammation is integral to the pathophysiology of MetS. Increased adiposity leads to increased cytokines and chemokines and dysregulated adipokines (Jialal & Devaraj, 2018). Almost every known molecule is modulated, with proven changes in tumor necrosis factor-α (TNF-α), interleukin (IL)-1, IL-6, IL-8, monocyte chemoattractant protein-1 (MCP-1), leptin, PAI-1, retinol binding protein 4 (RBP4), chemerin, serum amyloid A (SSA), C-reactive protein (CRP), lipopolysaccharide-binding protein (LBP), fetuin A, adiponectin and omentin-1 (Jung & Choi, 2014).
Research has increasingly focused on the interplay between the immune system and metabolic syndrome, recognizing that disruptions in immune-metabolic communication contribute to the progression of autoimmune diseases. The prevalence of MetS is notably higher in patients with autoimmune diseases, such as rheumatic diseases, systemic lupus erythematosus (SLE), ankylosing spondylitis, and vasculitis, with consequent elevated incidences of cardiovascular diseases (Medina et al., 2018; Müller et al., 2017; et al., Parker et al., 2010).

2.3.5 Hormonal Imbalances
Hormonal imbalances are also a major component contributing to the pathophysiology of metabolic syndrome. Recorded imbalances in the HPA axis, levels of cortisol, growth hormone, sex, and thyroid hormones affect fat distribution and metabolism, insulin sensitivity, and overall metabolic homeostasis (Pasquali et al., 2006). These effects also require the involvement of other hormones, including increased insulin, dysregulated catecholamines, decreased growth hormone, and altered androgen levels (Björntorp, 1996). 
PTH and osteocalcin also support critical functions needed for metabolic balance impacting calcium equilibrium, which plays a pivotal role in insulin production and lipid processing, while regulating glucose metabolism by increasing insulin secretion and sensitivity (Lee et al., 2007). PTH and osteocalcin are directly affected by vitamin D and vitamin K2 status

2.4 Clinical Manifestations of Metabolic Syndrome
2.4.1 Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus (T2DM)
	Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus has been intrinsically connected to three major risk factors, family history, obesity, and impaired glucose regulation. The latter two are integral part of the MetS definition, and are also the only considered modifiable. Epidemiological studies have shown that the relative risk  for diabetes in individuals with MetS ranges from a 3-fold to 20-fold increase (Aschner, 2010). This great impact has led to the conclusion that long-term undiagnosed and untreated MetS leads to the formation of T2DM. 
2.4.2 Cardiovascular Disease
Metabolic syndrome is considered a precursor to cardiovascular disease, significantly increasing the risk for CVD morbidity, mortality, and all-cause mortality (Mottillo et al., 2010). Each component of MetS, including obesity, insulin resistance, elevated blood pressure, high triglyceride levels, and reduced HDL cholesterol, independently increases the risk for cardiovascular disease (CVD). When these factors are combined, the rates and severity of the disease are significantly elevated, mediated by a spectrum of conditions including microvascular dysfunction, atherosclerosis, and cardiac dysfunction, leading to myocardial infarction and heart failure (Tune et al., 2017). 
2.4.3 MetS and other common chronic diseases 
 Visceral adiposity is strongly linked to hepatic fatty infiltration, with the level of fatty acids in the hepatic parenchyma being indirectly linked to MetS, as both cause and a consequence (Chalasani et al., 2012; Radu et al., 2023). According to current criteria, the prevalence of PCOS has risen to 20%, with a significant percentage of women with PCOS also exhibiting features of MetS and IR (Chen & Pang, 2021; Apridonidze et al., 2005). The relationship between serum uric acid levels and the components of metabolic syndrome is well-documented, with significant associations reported in numerous studies (Beyl et al., 2016; Ichikawa et al., 2011;  Choi & Ford, 2007). MetS has been associated with increased cancer mortality and prevalence, with strong evidence correlating it to colorectal cancer in both sexes, liver cancer in men, and pancreatic cancer in women. In cohort studies in men, the presence of MetS was associated with increased risk for liver, colorectal, and bladder cancer, while in women, it increases the risk for endometrial, pancreatic, breast, rectal, and colorectal cancer (Esposito et al., 2012).

2.5 Current Therapeutic Strategies 
Due to its multifactorial nature and dependence on lifestyle habits, metabolic syndrome requires a comprehensive approach targeting each component simultaneously. Interventions are widely based on lifestyle modifications, with emphasis on dietary changes, physical activity and management of obesity or increased BMI. Pharmacological treatments are utilized when these interventions are ineffective or in later stages of MetS and are based on controlling the signs and findings of the syndrome. 
Antihypertensives, such as angiotensin-converting enzyme inhibitors or angiotensin receptor blockers are prescribed to control hypertension (Whelton et al., 2018), cholesterol lowering drugs, including statins are fibrates are prescribed for dyslipidemia (Grundy et al., 2019), while antidiabetic, like metformin, sodium-glucose co-transporter-2 inhibitors and glucagon-like peptide-1 receptor agonists, are the main agents used to improve dysglycemia (Davies et al., 2022).
